AI研讨会：探索企业级应用与未来趋势

开场讨论：AI时代的学习、机遇与紧迫感

Dave Wessinger: And my, kind of, two major investors in Dragonair and Hillman Friedman.

Dave Wessinger: 我的两大主要投资者，Dragoneer（Dragoneer投资集团：一家专注于科技领域的成长型股权投资公司）和Hellman & Friedman（Hellman & Friedman：一家全球领先的私募股权投资公司）。

Dave Wessinger: Spend more time trying to get me connected with every single person that's moving well, or better or differently in AI, so I can learn from that.

Dave Wessinger: 他们花了很多时间，试图让我与每一个在AI领域做得好、更好或与众不同的人建立联系，以便我能从中学习。

Dave Wessinger: It's a massive learning journey, and every day could be spent with yet another company understanding their journey.

Dave Wessinger: 这是一个巨大的学习过程，每天都可以花在了解另一家公司的发展历程上。

Dave Wessinger: And they tend to connect me with ones that have had some reasonable success.

Dave Wessinger: 他们倾向于把我介绍给那些已经取得一定成功的公司。

Dave Wessinger: And so, I'll just speak to one that's actually, um, connected to healthcare. This is a little more financial, but do have some healthcare customers, and then I'll talk about a healthcare company.

Dave Wessinger: 所以，我先谈一个与医疗健康相关的例子。这家公司更偏向金融领域，但确实有一些医疗客户，之后我再谈一家纯粹的医疗公司。

Dave Wessinger: Um, the one that I saw was…. It's a really interesting concept, and I think as I talk about other organizations.

Dave Wessinger: 我看到的那家公司……它的概念非常有趣，我认为在我谈论其他组织时也是如此。

Dave Wessinger: I'm largely talking about solutions they deliver to the market as the priority, but invariably, I think when we think about what might be delivered to a market.

Dave Wessinger: 我主要谈论的是他们向市场提供的解决方案，但当我们思考可能向市场交付什么时，情况总是如此。

Dave Wessinger: In our own rights, our internal stuff, we're consuming others' solutions. So it's the same thing, just upside down.

Dave Wessinger: 就我们自身而言，我们的内部系统也在使用他人的解决方案。所以这其实是同一件事，只是角度不同。

Dave Wessinger: And the thing that they've done well, as an organization, they struggled to deliver AI to the market.

Dave Wessinger: 他们作为一个组织做得很好的一点是，他们曾努力将AI推向市场，但遇到了困难。

Dave Wessinger: Um, and…. I think what I recognize the challenge with, they at least iterated, was….

Dave Wessinger: 我认为我认识到的挑战在于，他们至少进行了迭代……

Dave Wessinger: They've… they're moving really well in AI now, in the end market. Their revenue doubled year over year.

Dave Wessinger: 他们现在在AI领域，在终端市场上发展得非常好。他们的收入同比增长了一倍。

Dave Wessinger: They acquired an AI company, accelerated some of their work, and they basically have been building agents for the last 6 months.

Dave Wessinger: 他们收购了一家AI公司，加速了部分工作，并且在过去6个月里一直在构建AI智能体（AI agents：能自主感知环境、决策并执行任务的智能程序）。

Dave Wessinger: And driving a ton of opportunity into the business. And so they sell it, it's an orchestration layer for their customers.

Dave Wessinger: 这为业务带来了大量机会。他们销售的是一个为其客户服务的编排层（orchestration layer：用于自动化和协调复杂系统或服务之间工作流的技术层）。

Dave Wessinger: They productionized it versus give their end customers an opportunity to build their own agents.

Dave Wessinger: 他们将其产品化，而不是让终端客户有机会自己构建智能体。

Dave Wessinger: And they've done extremely well, and I think doubling revenue in a given year is pretty incredible, actually.

Dave Wessinger: 他们做得非常出色，我认为在一年内实现收入翻倍确实是相当了不起的成就。

Dave Wessinger: In terms of an outcome. So that's really positive. The one takeaway for me there was.

Dave Wessinger: 从结果来看，这非常积极。我从中得到的一个启示是。

Dave Wessinger: He had challenged his own team, really smart, capable people. To move with agents and build it themselves.

Dave Wessinger: 他曾挑战自己的团队，那些非常聪明、有能力的人，让他们利用智能体自己构建解决方案。

Dave Wessinger: And he gave them a certain amount of time before he had to go outside and acquire it, and basically they got.

Dave Wessinger: 他给了他们一定的时间，之后他不得不向外部寻求并收购技术，基本上他们做到了。

Dave Wessinger: They weren't able to get to the point where you thought they could have, and so he had to acquire.

Dave Wessinger: 他们没能达到他预期的水平，所以他最终不得不进行收购。

Dave Wessinger: And I guess my takeaway from that is no more than.

Dave Wessinger: 我想我从中得到的启示无非是。

Dave Wessinger: If we're not taking time to sharpen the saw and learn and grow, we're gonna be always caught up with the problems of the day and the priorities of what's gonna pull us back.

Dave Wessinger: 如果我们不花时间磨砺自己、学习和成长，我们就会永远被日常问题和那些拖后腿的优先事项所困扰。

Dave Wessinger: And I think getting focused on where we need to go is a lot of courage from leadership, is a lot of courage from all of us.

Dave Wessinger: 我认为，专注于我们需要前进的方向，需要领导层和我们所有人的巨大勇气。

Dave Wessinger: And I think it's not what you say yes to, it's what you say no to.

Dave Wessinger: 而且我认为，关键不在于你答应了什么，而在于你拒绝了什么。

Dave Wessinger: And I think the one thing we hear around this organization a lot.

Dave Wessinger: 我认为我们在这个组织里经常听到的一件事是。

Dave Wessinger: Is there's a lot of priorities, and the priorities come down to leadership. And if we're not really clear.

Dave Wessinger: 有太多的优先事项，而这些优先事项最终都归结于领导层。如果我们不非常清楚。

Dave Wessinger: With where we need to go, what we need to choose, we're not gonna make that progress. No matter how much learning we do today.

Dave Wessinger: 我们需要去向何方，需要做出何种选择，我们就无法取得进步。无论我们今天学习了多少。

Dave Wessinger: We need to create space, um, and that's gonna be hard, and it's gonna be hard to stomach sometimes, because that will deviate from our current plans.

Dave Wessinger: 我们需要创造空间，这会很困难，有时甚至难以接受，因为它会偏离我们当前的计划。

Dave Wessinger: But, uh, that's kind of one example. I think…. The other one is, um, and this is a little bit external, talking to some companies that are leveraging AI to drive their growth.

Dave Wessinger: 但这就是一个例子。我认为……另一个例子，这稍微有点外部视角，是关于一些利用AI来驱动其在医疗健康领域增长的公司。

Dave Wessinger: In healthcare. And one example was, there's a company that has built an orchestration layer.

Dave Wessinger: 在医疗健康领域。一个例子是，有一家公司在我们的应用程序之上构建了一个编排层。

Dave Wessinger: On top of our application, that does two things. One, gives end users an ability to automate all of their manual processes.

Dave Wessinger: 它能做两件事。第一，让最终用户能够自动化他们所有的手动流程。

Dave Wessinger: So they call it agents… Agent Operating Procedures. And they're building a ton of them, on top of our application.

Dave Wessinger: 他们称之为智能体……智能体操作程序。他们在我们的应用程序之上构建了大量的这类程序。

Dave Wessinger: So what's interesting out of that is it's not… it's not human-centered design. It's machine-centered design.

Dave Wessinger: 有趣的是，这不再是以人为本的设计，而是以机器为中心的设计。

Dave Wessinger: Kind of interesting. Um, kind of moving away from that. And then where they've taken some opportunity, they've gone and they've created Chrome extensions on top of our app to create a side-by-side workflow where customers can create a lot of intelligence in this Chrome extension.

Dave Wessinger: 这很有趣，有点偏离了传统模式。然后他们抓住了一些机会，在我们的应用之上创建了Chrome扩展程序，形成了一个并行的工作流，客户可以在这个Chrome扩展中创造出很多智能功能。

Dave Wessinger: On top of our application. So what's…. What's it? And they're making really nice progress, kind of….

Dave Wessinger: 在我们的应用程序之上。所以……这是什么？他们正在取得非常好的进展，可以说……

Dave Wessinger: Let's say, to some extent, pre-revenue, but starting to take off, because it's obviously solving a big problem.

Dave Wessinger: 在某种程度上，他们还处于营收前阶段，但已经开始起飞，因为它显然解决了一个大问题。

Dave Wessinger: And if it's not clear in every boardroom, the ask is more AI, more AI, more AI, and so if somebody's solving that, and it's not us, uh, that could be problematic, and so it does drive you to a sense of urgency and pace to start to deliver on that need. So, two different examples.

Dave Wessinger: 如果在每个董事会里还不清楚的话，那么需求就是更多的AI，更多的AI，更多的AI。所以如果有人在解决这个问题，而那个人不是我们，那可能会很麻烦。这确实会驱使你产生一种紧迫感和节奏感，去开始满足这种需求。所以，这是两个不同的例子。

Dave Wessinger: Of companies leveraging more of an AI. One wasn't AI-native, and the other one is.

Dave Wessinger: 关于公司如何更多地利用AI。一个不是AI原生公司，另一个则是。

Dave Wessinger: Um, and then the question is, you know, how do you compete against that, and how do you think about that?

Dave Wessinger: 那么问题来了，你如何与他们竞争，你如何看待这个问题？

Dave Wessinger: And then internally, think about this for a moment. We're trying to deliver to our customers AI-powered solutions is where we would like to be.

Dave Wessinger: 然后在内部，思考一下。我们希望能够为客户提供AI驱动的解决方案。

Dave Wessinger: Our vendors internally that you deal with, Alan, are trying to.

Dave Wessinger: Alan，你所接触的我们内部的供应商，他们也在努力。

Dave Wessinger: Deliver AI to us, and they tend to be in their segments, so whether it's finance, or sales, or product, or.

Dave Wessinger: 向我们提供AI，而且他们通常专注于各自的领域，无论是金融、销售、产品，还是其他。

Dave Wessinger: Or services, or otherwise. But we have to put Humpty Dumpty together in some way, shape, or form to deliver a seamless experience and process for our own employees, so….

Dave Wessinger: 或者是服务或其他方面。但我们必须以某种方式将这些零散的部分整合起来，为我们自己的员工提供无缝的体验和流程，所以……

Dave Wessinger: It's kind of hard to think about single-source AI vendors. And that's why things like Copilot or orchestration layers take off, is because they do go across so many different applications and drive a ton of efficiency in the business, so….

Dave Wessinger: 很难想象只依赖单一来源的AI供应商。这就是为什么像Copilot或编排层这样的东西会流行起来，因为它们确实能够跨越许多不同的应用程序，并为业务带来巨大的效率提升，所以……

Dave Wessinger: There's just a few examples that, uh, have kind of a….

Dave Wessinger: 这里只是几个例子，它们都有一种……

Dave Wessinger: It does drive a sense of urgency in terms of the….

Dave Wessinger: 它确实在……方面带来了一种紧迫感。

Dave Wessinger: These things aren't just… we're not just talking about them in theory, they're real.

Dave Wessinger: 这些事情不仅仅是……我们不只是在理论上谈论它们，它们是真实存在的。

Dave Wessinger: They're starting to impact businesses. Uh, and its material. Uh, so I think it's an opportunity internally, but also externally. One doesn't go without the other.

Dave Wessinger: 它们已经开始影响企业，而且是实质性的影响。所以我认为这既是内部的机会，也是外部的机会。两者相辅相成。

Alan Missen: Yeah, those are great examples, Dave. I think your point around, sort of.

Alan Missen: 是的，Dave，这些例子很棒。我认为你关于……的观点。

Alan Missen: You know, committed time to learn, right? And that sort of ruthless prioritization.

Alan Missen: 你知道，投入时间去学习，对吧？以及那种坚决的优先级排序。

Alan Missen: The combination of those two, I think, is a very powerful comment that we really need to take seriously on the back end of today, frankly. I think it's a great point, well made.

Alan Missen: 我认为这两者的结合是一个非常有力的观点，坦白说，我们今天结束后真的需要认真对待。这是一个很好的观点，说得很好。

Dave Wessinger: Alan, how do you… let me ask you a question as we're kind of going back and forth. We, as everybody here knows, or should know, we've had a….

Dave Wessinger: Alan，你如何……在我们来回讨论的时候，我问你一个问题。我们，在座的各位都知道，或者应该知道，我们有一个……

Alan Missen: Yeah, I think… I think we're kind of at the beginning of the journey, um, in all honesty, but I… and I do think that that's a….

Alan Missen: 是的，我认为……坦白说，我们才刚刚开始这段旅程，但我……我确实认为这是一个……

Dave Wessinger: A meaningful effort around P2C. And as you think about what we're doing design-wise, business process engineering or business process modeling.

Dave Wessinger: 围绕P2C（Product-to-Cash：从产品到现金，指企业从产品开发到最终收到客户付款的整个业务流程）的一项有意义的努力。当你思考我们在设计方面所做的工作，无论是业务流程工程还是业务流程建模。

Dave Wessinger: Is a lot around how humans use a solution, and we think about, you know, Salesforce or other components that might be in there, and NetSuite.

Dave Wessinger: 很多都是围绕人类如何使用一个解决方案，我们会考虑到Salesforce（赛富时：一家提供客户关系管理软件和服务的公司）或其他可能包含在内的组件，以及NetSuite（甲骨文公司旗下的云ERP软件）。

Dave Wessinger: How do you think about AI as it relates to designing differently.

Dave Wessinger: 你如何看待AI在不同设计方法中的应用？

Dave Wessinger: For the things that we traditionally would focus on, how does a human do X, and how do we make it better?

Dave Wessinger: 对于我们传统上关注的事情，比如人类如何完成某项任务X，以及我们如何改进它？

Dave Wessinger: How do you think differently about using agents, or thinking differently about AI in just re-engineering the process?

Dave Wessinger: 在仅仅是重新设计流程方面，你对使用智能体或对AI有何不同的看法？

Alan Missen: An area we're evolving… we're trying to evolve quite… quite quickly, Dave. I think….

Alan Missen: Dave，这是一个我们正在努力……非常、非常快速发展的领域。我认为……

Alan Missen: If we look at, sort of, the traditional way to build… to deliver those big transformational projects, you're right, you sort of scope it, you build it, you test it, you go live.

Alan Missen: 如果我们看传统的方式来构建……来交付那些大型转型项目，你说得对，你通常是先确定范围，然后构建，测试，最后上线。

Alan Missen: And we're sort of two-thirds of the way down that journey, and all of a sudden, there's a capability available to us that wasn't when we started the project.

Alan Missen: 我们大概走完了这个过程的三分之二，然后突然之间，出现了一种我们项目开始时没有的能力。

Dave Wessinger: Yeah.

Dave Wessinger: 是的。

Alan Missen: Um, and so right now, we are sort of actively looking at, are there 3 or 4 areas within P2C.

Alan Missen: 所以现在，我们正在积极地研究，在P2C（产品到现金）流程中是否有三到四个领域。

Alan Missen: That we can start leveraging this right away. So it's not just about this new idea that's down the road that we'll go tackle. It's like, we've got stuff that is in flight.

Alan Missen: 我们可以立即开始利用这项技术。所以这不仅仅是关于未来某个新想法，而是我们手头正在进行的项目。

Alan Missen: How do we start thinking about applying it right now? So a great one is an….

Alan Missen: 我们如何开始思考立即应用它？一个很好的例子是……

Alan Missen: I think we showed it at the SLT, and I know it's a passionate one for you, is….

Alan Missen: 我想我们在SLT（Senior Leadership Team：高级领导团队）会议上展示过，而且我知道你对此充满热情，那就是……

Alan Missen: Could we get an agent to build a quote for a customer for Go Live in November? Could we actually have that ready?

Alan Missen: 我们能否让一个智能体为客户在11月上线时生成一份报价？我们真的能准备好吗？

Alan Missen: Right? And so we're really kind of pushing the envelope on that. And I think there's….

Alan Missen: 对吧？所以我们真的在挑战极限。而且我认为……

Alan Missen: 3 or 4 sort of agentic ideas, sort of on the back end of the finance side.

Alan Missen: 在财务后端，有三到四个类似智能体的想法。

Alan Missen: As well, that we're starting to play around with is to say, can we get those in for November 1st as well? So.

Alan Missen: 我们也开始尝试，看看能否在11月1日之前也把它们实现。所以。

Alan Missen: It's a little scary, because we're trying to, like, change scope as we're sort of building the plane.

Alan Missen: 这有点吓人，因为我们就像是在造飞机的同时试图改变它的设计范围。

Alan Missen: Uh, but those are some of the things we're thinking about, uh, within, say, say, PSC around that idea.

Alan Missen: 但这些是我们正在考虑的一些事情，比如在PSC（项目指导委员会）内部围绕这个想法进行讨论。

Dave Wessinger: Very good. Yeah, it's exciting. Your point is very interesting in that….

Dave Wessinger: 非常好。是的，这很令人兴奋。你的观点非常有趣，在于……

Dave Wessinger: You know, the advancements in 6 months, never mind 24 hours.

Dave Wessinger: 你知道，六个月内的进步，更不用说24小时了。

Dave Wessinger: Are just… it's unsettling how… the pace of change, and I think Mike talked about a 5-year time horizon.

Dave Wessinger: 简直是……变革的速度令人不安，我想Mike谈到了一个五年的时间跨度。

Dave Wessinger: Um, you know, disruption of the cloud really took 10-plus years.

Dave Wessinger: 你知道，云计算的颠覆真正花了十年以上的时间。

Dave Wessinger: Disruption here is…. Barely measured in years. I mean, two, three years out, what we see today as normal is gonna be….

Dave Wessinger: 这里的颠覆……几乎不能用年来衡量。我的意思是，两三年后，我们今天视为正常的东西将会……

Dave Wessinger: It's gonna feel like it was 50 years ago history. It's pretty incredible.

Dave Wessinger: 感觉就像是50年前的历史。这真是太不可思议了。

Alan Missen: Yeah. And I think the other comment you made, which is really interesting, is some of the stuff that you're seeing around, sort of, the bigger platforms, it's like the attack vector.

Alan Missen: 是的。而且我认为你提出的另一个评论也很有趣，就是你看到的一些关于大型平台的情况，它就像是攻击向量。

Alan Missen: For some of the innovations, actually, kind of on the edges, right? It's not necessarily sort of the… always the big players who are coming at you, it's the small, innovative.

Alan Missen: 对于一些创新来说，实际上是在边缘地带，对吧？不一定总是那些大公司来挑战你，而是那些小而创新的公司。

Alan Missen: Company that's sort of hitting it around the edges of what sort of we're doing, and that's… that's really an interesting.

Alan Missen: 公司正在我们所做事情的边缘地带进行冲击，这……这确实是一个有趣的现象。

Alan Missen: Dynamic for us to wrap our head around. And then the other comment you made around, sort of.

Alan Missen: 动态，需要我们去理解。然后你还提到了另一个评论，关于……

Alan Missen: Um, there's a data point that's… there's a data point that suggests right now.

Alan Missen: 有一个数据点……有一个数据点表明，现在。

Alan Missen: 我认为，你知道，这……你说得对，现在每个供应商都在敲我们的门，说，你们需要看看我们的产品。

Dave Wessinger: Let me share with you the why behind that. Um, and it really starts with, if you think about enterprise value, is kind of a key driver for a lot of folks.

Dave Wessinger: 让我与你分享这背后的原因。这实际上始于，如果你考虑到企业价值，它对很多人来说是一个关键驱动因素。

Dave Wessinger: You sit in a boardroom, and you talk to… and this came up a little bit, but more so, kind of, after.

Dave Wessinger: 你坐在董事会里，和……谈话，这个问题稍微被提及，但更多的是在之后。

Dave Wessinger: We had this conversation of, you know. What if we do well, or what if we do poorly? Let's just play out kind of a few scenarios.

Dave Wessinger: 我们进行了这样的对话，你知道的。如果我们做得好会怎样？或者如果我们做得不好会怎样？让我们来推演几种情景。

Dave Wessinger: Um, and if… if we do poorly, we could be half the value today.

Dave Wessinger: 如果……如果我们做得不好，我们的价值可能会是今天的一半。

Dave Wessinger: Six months from now. Half of our value.

Aakif Shaik: Okay, awesome. Sweet. Alright, hello everyone. My name is Akif Sheikh. I am a business transformation co-op in the SDO.

Aakif Shaik: 好的，太棒了。很好。大家好。我叫Akif Sheikh。我是SDO（战略交付办公室）的一名业务转型实习生。

Aakif Shaik: And over the past few weeks, I've been working on building an AI-powered co-pilot agent that integrates with Copilot Studio and Power Automate.

Aakif Shaik: 在过去几周里，我一直在致力于构建一个与Copilot Studio和Power Automate集成的AI驱动的Copilot智能体。

Aakif Shaik: And for those of you who aren't familiar with AHA, it is a product or a project management tool that teams use to be able to track and manage their work.

Aakif Shaik: 对于那些不熟悉Aha!的人来说，它是一个产品或项目管理工具，团队用它来跟踪和管理他们的工作。

Aakif Shaik: And so, within the SDO, we essentially use AHA to track and manage our key initiatives, like the go-to markets and the product-to-cash program.

Aakif Shaik: 因此，在SDO内部，我们主要使用Aha!来跟踪和管理我们的关键举措，比如市场推广（go-to-market）和产品到现金（product-to-cash）项目。

Aakif Shaik: And so the problem that I was really focused on was, how can I make it easier for people, whether they're a program manager or someone within the team who's trying to access and get a quick update, to be able to use an AI-powered assistant to do that. And so, if you've ever found yourself thinking, hey, I just want a quick status update without jumping between different tools.

Aakif Shaik: 我真正关注的问题是，如何让人们，无论是项目经理还是团队中试图获取快速更新的成员，能够更轻松地使用AI驱动的助手来完成这项工作。所以，如果你曾发现自己想，“嘿，我只想快速了解状态，而不想在不同工具之间切换”。

Aakif Shaik: Then this one's for you. And so, where we're at on our current journey is, right at that pilot stage, where we're testing out use cases.

Aakif Shaik: 那么这个就是为你准备的。我们目前的旅程正处于试点阶段，我们正在测试用例。

Aakif Shaik: As well as adding additional use cases, and so once we get to that full functionality, is when we want to move to the full adoption.

Aakif Shaik: 同时也在增加额外的用例，一旦我们实现了全部功能，我们就会转向全面采用。

Aakif Shaik: And so, going to the demo stage. Here is a little bit of a walkthrough of what the UI interface looks like for Copilot Studio.

Aakif Shaik: 那么，进入演示阶段。这里是Copilot Studio用户界面（UI）的一个简要介绍。

Aakif Shaik: And as you can see here, I'm going to start off by giving it a simple prompt by asking it, hey, what are the activities that are currently due this week?

Aakif Shaik: 正如你在这里看到的，我将从一个简单的提示开始，问它：“嘿，本周有哪些活动到期？”

Aakif Shaik: Right? And so, once I go ahead and do that, you can see on the left side of the screen that it starts to execute a flow. And so what this co-pilot agent is currently doing is using Power Automate, which is integrated with Araha, to pull in information on activities that are currently due this week.

Aakif Shaik: 对吧？一旦我这样做，你可以在屏幕左侧看到它开始执行一个流程。这个Copilot智能体目前正在做的是使用与Aha!集成的Power Automate，来提取本周到期的活动信息。

Aakif Shaik: 好了，它特别关注GTM（Go-to-Market：市场推广）项目，并向我们显示了本周到期的活动名称及其截止日期。

So I'm gonna go ahead and give it another prompt now, asking it, I want to know the status of a particular activity.

Aakif Shaik: 这很棒，那么让我们再进一步，说：“嘿，我们如何获取每个活动的具体细节？”对吧？所以我现在要给它另一个提示，问它：“我想知道某个特定活动的状态。”

Aakif Shaik: So, once again, you can see on the left side there, it's executing a different flow now, um, which is asking for which activity would I like to check. And so, I want to give it the name of that particular activity.

Aakif Shaik: 所以，再次，你可以在左侧看到，它现在正在执行一个不同的流程，询问我想检查哪个活动。因此，我要告诉它那个特定活动的名称。

Aakif Shaik: And once I do that, that's when it starts to execute a different flow.

Aakif Shaik: 一旦我这样做了，它就会开始执行一个不同的流程。

Aakif Shaik: And so now in this flow, the output is going to be different, because it is going to be focused on this particular activity and getting us the status updates. So here we go, gives us the name, what the current status is.

Aakif Shaik: 所以现在在这个流程中，输出将会不同，因为它将专注于这个特定的活动并为我们获取状态更新。好了，它给出了名称，当前的状态是什么。

Aakif Shaik: What the due date is, as well as who it is assigned to.

Aakif Shaik: 截止日期是什么，以及分配给了谁。

Aakif Shaik: And so, this is what the current functionality of the agent looks like, and so going a little bit of what's under the hood.

Aakif Shaik: 这就是这个智能体当前的功能。现在我们来看看它的内部工作原理。

Aakif Shaik: If you want to add additional functionalities, you essentially add them as topics until you start off with a trigger, and then a question.

Aakif Shaik: 如果你想添加额外的功能，你基本上是将它们作为主题添加，直到你从一个触发器开始，然后是一个问题。

Aakif Shaik: And then the action. So this is where you want to integrate your Power Automate flow with it. And lastly, you have your output message.

Aakif Shaik: 然后是动作。这就是你想要将Power Automate流程与之集成的地方。最后，你会有你的输出信息。

Aakif Shaik: And so the same thing goes, um, you know, for the other flow as well, which covers what is due this week. And so, this trigger is really important because this is what the agent uses to differentiate on what your ask is.

Aakif Shaik: 同样地，对于另一个流程也是如此，它涵盖了本周到期的任务。这个触发器非常重要，因为智能体用它来区分你的请求是什么。

Aakif Shaik: And so, um, once again, you have your flow, as well as your final message. And so, for those of you that are curious to see, you know, what this Power Automate flow looks like, feel free to reach out, and I'll be happy to give you a walkthrough after this call as well.

Aakif Shaik: 所以，再次，你有你的流程，以及你的最终信息。对于那些好奇想看看这个Power Automate流程是什么样子的朋友，请随时联系我，我很乐意在这次通话后也给你们做一个演示。

Aakif Shaik: So now, moving on to, you know, really talking about impact, right? And so what this tool really allows teams to do is transform how they access project updates. So having this AI-powered assistant allows you to just, you know, minimize the use of switching over different tools, as well as digging through different dashboards.

Aakif Shaik: 现在，我们来谈谈影响，对吧？这个工具真正让团队能够改变他们获取项目更新的方式。拥有这个AI驱动的助手，可以让你减少在不同工具之间切换的次数，以及在不同仪表盘中挖掘信息的麻烦。

Aakif Shaik: And actually just be able to get detailed, focused answers through a simple question.

Aakif Shaik: 并且能够通过一个简单的问题获得详细、集中的答案。

Aakif Shaik: Now, the lessons learned for me in this journey were definitely to start small and build iteratively. So following up on what Dave had said earlier, it was, you know, starting off with a simple use case, testing out a sample set of data, and continuously building on that to make sure that it didn't get overwhelmed.

Aakif Shaik: 在这次旅程中，我学到的教训绝对是從小處著手，迭代構建。接續Dave之前所說的，就是從一個簡單的用例開始，測試一組樣本數據，並在此基礎上不斷構建，以確保不會不堪重負。

Aakif Shaik: And then, you know, getting to the stage where we're at, where we're working with all of the complex data.

Aakif Shaik: 然后，你知道，进入我们现在的阶段，我们正在处理所有复杂的数据。

Aakif Shaik: Now, how we can help others at PCC, so teams can definitely use, um, you know, Copilot agents for various purposes, and so one thing I can think of would be for the product team to be able to, you know, build a co-pilot agent that integrates with their product roadmap, so that teams can get status of where they're at in the entire product roadmap journey.

Aakif Shaik: 现在，我们如何能帮助PCC（PointClickCare）的其他人，团队绝对可以出于各种目的使用Copilot智能体。我能想到的一个例子是，产品团队可以构建一个与他们的产品路线图集成的Copilot智能体，这样团队就能了解他们在整个产品路线图旅程中的进展状态。

Aakif Shaik: This can also be useful for teams that use Jira, so be able to get quick status updates on what the JIRA, um, you know.

Aakif Shaik: 这对于使用Jira（一款流行的项目管理和问题跟踪软件）的团队也很有用，可以快速获取Jira的状态更新。

Aakif Shaik: Dashboard basically states. And lastly, the responsible use of AI. So, this project aligns with the responsible AI guidelines.

Sonal Misra: 客户在采用该产品之前所面临的问题。因此，该模型能够识别出超越手动范围的代码、更高的风险和低效的工作流程，这些都是团队可以立即采取行动的洞察。

Sonal Misra: 此外，为了识别指标和证据点，我能够输入提示，要求你列出访谈中提供的数字证据或绩效指标。

Sonal Misra: This can be done by clicking on the three dots on the left-hand side panel beside your email address.

Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq: 大家好！在我们等待下一位演讲者准备的时候，我有一个问题要问大家。

Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq: 事实还是虚构？AI可以承担法律责任。在聊天中告诉我你认为答案是什么。

Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq: 我希望我有一些《危险边缘》的音乐。哦，是的，还没有。假的，不是真的，虚构的，不。

Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq: 有人说，Drew，我看到了很多虚构的东西，不可能。

Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq: AI的试点，真正的AI，不。好的！很多非常有趣的回答，但似乎……你能起诉AI吗，Marina在问。好的，所以……

Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq: If you haven't responded yet, and you're thinking about the question, we will tell you what the answer is.

Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq: 如果你还没有回答，并且正在思考这个问题，我们会告诉你答案是什么。

Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq: The answer is that this is fiction. Um, AI is not a separate legal entity, so it can't be held responsible.

Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq: 答案是，这是虚构的。AI不是一个独立的法律实体，所以它不能承担责任。

Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq: And there's actually really interesting stories about this in the news over the last few years. One of the ones that sticks out for me is a story about Air Canada and its chatbot.

Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq: 过去几年新闻里其实有很多关于这个的有趣故事。其中一个让我印象深刻的是关于加拿大航空公司及其聊天机器人的故事。

Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq: Keki，你记得听过那个故事吗？

Ketki Yennemadi: 是的，我模糊地记得一些。它上过新闻，不是吗？

Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq: Yes, I was. Okay, so basically what happened was, in 2022, Air Canada had a chatbot on its website.

Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq: 是的，我记得。好的，基本上是这样的，2022年，加拿大航空公司在其网站上有一个聊天机器人。

Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq: And a customer went in and asked about a particular discount. The chatbot said that it could be honored.

Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq: 一位顾客进去询问一个特定的折扣。聊天机器人说可以兑现。

Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq: But it turns out that Air Canada said that it shouldn't. And so they wouldn't want to honor the discount, and when they were taken to court.

Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq: 但结果是加拿大航空公司说不应该兑现。所以他们不想兑现这个折扣，当他们被起诉到法庭时。

Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq: The court actually ruled against them. They basically said, it's your website, the chatbot's on your website, so you're responsible for whatever it puts out. And so then they were required to not only pay.

Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq: 法院实际上判他们败诉。他们基本上说，这是你们的网站，聊天机器人在你们的网站上，所以你们要对它发布的一切负责。因此，他们不仅被要求支付。

Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq: What the difference was, but also legal fees, etc. So, I think the story behind this is that.

Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq: 差价，还要支付律师费等。所以，我认为这背后的故事是。

Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq: 你要确保它接受了适当信息的训练，这样当有人提问时，它能提取正确的内容。

Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq: And then in general, when you're using AI, you want to make sure you're validating the output before you use it. And you'll hear us talk about RAI throughout all of them.

Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq: 总的来说，当你使用AI时，你要确保在使用之前验证输出。你会听到我们在所有这些中都谈到RAI（负责任的AI）。

Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq: 是的，Mike，我们接下来就要讲那个故事，关于这个臭名昭著的法律事件。所以，Keck，你想给我们讲讲吗？

Ketki Yennemadi: 是的。哦，是的！是的，那是一个非常有趣的事件。我记得，2023年有一个臭名昭著的法律事件，一位纽约律师使用ChatGPT起草了一份法庭文件。

Ketki Yennemadi: And he actually ended up citing 6 completely fabricated legal cases. All of these cases were hallucinated.

Ketki Yennemadi: 他最终引用了6个完全捏造的法律案例。所有这些案例都是AI幻觉的结果。

Ketki Yennemadi: And what we mean by hallucination, AI does that quite a bit, is that they were completely made up by AI, they just did not exist.

Ketki Yennemadi: 我们所说的幻觉，AI经常这样做，就是它们完全是AI编造出来的，根本不存在。

Ketki Yennemadi: And the judge had to sanction the lawyer. The courts even emphasized that while using AI, which is not inherently wrong, lawyers do have a duty to verify the accuracy of their filing and what they are citing.

Ketki Yennemadi: 法官不得不制裁这位律师。法院甚至强调，虽然使用AI本身并没有错，但律师有责任核实他们提交文件的准确性以及他们引用的内容。

Ketki Yennemadi: Uh, in those filings. So it was a very, very interesting incident, and both the lawyer and his colleague were actually sanctioned in that case.

Ketki Yennemadi: 在那些文件中。所以这是一个非常、非常有趣的事件，在那起案件中，律师和他的同事都受到了制裁。

Ketki Yennemadi: 他们还必须支付罚款。所以是的，非常有趣的案例。

Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq: 能力越大，责任越大，对吧？虽然是另一部电影，但在这里也挺相关的。是的，Tim，你说得对，你需要有人在环（human in the loop），对吧？这是我们使用AI时非常重要的一部分。

kristy liu: 这意味着调查可能需要更长的时间，因为我们需要来回切换。

kristy liu: Sometimes we need to run multiple queries in different platforms and try to piece everything together manually.

kristy liu: 有时我们需要在不同的平台上运行多个查询，并尝试手动将所有信息拼凑在一起。

kristy liu: We realized the challenge, and we can do something to improve it. Therefore, we purchased ReliaQuest.

kristy liu: 我们意识到了这个挑战，并且我们可以做些什么来改进它。因此，我们购买了ReliaQuest。

kristy liu: And we feed all the log sources into ReliaQuest. Now relyQuest becomes the central platform. It posts the data from all these tools, and it uses AI to normalize the data.

kristy liu: 我们将所有的日志源输入到ReliaQuest中。现在ReliaQuest成为了中心平台。它发布来自所有这些工具的数据，并使用AI来规范化数据。

kristy liu: And we can just work from one place. Because of that, investigation time has dropped from 45 minutes.

kristy liu: 我们就可以在一个地方工作。因此，调查时间从45分钟减少了。

kristy liu: 在许多情况下，降至约20分钟。我们现在有了可重复使用的剧本和清晰的流程，这使得团队中的任何人，无论他们是新手还是经验丰富，都能更容易地工作。

kristy liu: This slide shows how ReliaQuest uses Agenta AI to investigate alerts.

kristy liu: 这张幻灯片展示了ReliaQuest如何使用智能体AI来调查警报。

kristy liu: When an alert comes in, the process starts with the planner component.

kristy liu: 当警报传来时，流程从规划器组件开始。

kristy liu: It's like the brain of the system. Uh, it looks at the context around the alert.

kristy liu: 它就像系统的大脑。它会查看警报的上下文。

kristy liu: 它了解环境，以及是否有任何类似的过去警报等等。

kristy liu: Then it will decide how to investigate it. After the planner stage, it hands off to the part of the system that actually takes actions.

kristy liu: 然后它会决定如何调查。在规划阶段之后，它会把任务交给系统中实际采取行动的部分。

kristy liu: This part runs the searches. Uses the tools and does the heavy lifting to carry out the investigation. Now, depending on what happens during the process.

kristy liu: 这部分负责运行搜索，使用工具并承担繁重的工作来执行调查。现在，根据过程中发生的情况。

kristy liu: We get one of the three possible outcomes. If the result is unclear, or something doesn't look right, the system goes back to the planner and to rethink the approach.

kristy liu: 我们会得到三种可能的结果之一。如果结果不清楚，或者有什么看起来不对劲，系统会回到规划器重新思考方法。

kristy liu: If everything looks good, it builds a reusable playbook. If it's not a real threat, it marks it as a false positive.

kristy liu: 如果一切看起来都很好，它会构建一个可重复使用的剧本。如果不是真正的威胁，它会将其标记为误报。

kristy liu: This is how a gentle AI process works at a high level, from planning to action to outcome.

kristy liu: 这就是智能AI流程在高层次上的工作方式，从规划到行动再到结果。

用例7：Daisy Dool - AI赋能客户规划流程

Daisy Dool: Perfect. Thank you. Let me just share my screen.

Daisy Dool: 完美。谢谢你。我这就分享我的屏幕。

Daisy Dool: Fantastic. Thank you, everybody, for your patience, and a warm hello from me.

Daisy Dool: 太棒了。谢谢大家的耐心等待，我向大家致以热烈的问候。

Daisy Dool: I am Daisy, and I'm an Enablement Program Manager. I design and manage programs and empower customer-facing teams, like sales and customer success, so they can do their best work. My focus is on driving efficiency, boosting productivity, and creating learning experiences that truly support our revenue goals.

Daisy Dool: 我是Daisy，一名赋能项目经理。我设计和管理项目，并赋能面向客户的团队，如销售和客户成功团队，让他们能做到最好。我的重点是提高效率、提升生产力，并创造真正支持我们收入目标的学习体验。

Daisy Dool: Whether that's increasing pipeline, improving customer retention, or enabling teams to confidently navigate complex processes.

Daisy Dool: 无论是增加销售管道、提高客户保留率，还是让团队能够自信地应对复杂流程。

Daisy Dool: I work cross-functionally with sales, customer success, professional services, product and marketing, to build scalable training paths, launch new tools, and workflows, and ensure teams have what they need at the right time.

Daisy Dool: 我与销售、客户成功、专业服务、产品和市场营销等部门跨职能合作，构建可扩展的培训路径，推出新工具和工作流程，并确保团队在正确的时间获得所需的支持。

Daisy Dool: To succeed with their customers. Today, I'm sharing how we reimagined a core workflow using AI.

Daisy Dool: 与他们的客户一起成功。今天，我将分享我们如何使用AI重新构想一个核心工作流程。

Daisy Dool: Specifically. How we helped account executives reclaim hours of planning time by using tools they already have.

Daisy Dool: 具体来说，我们如何通过使用他们已有的工具，帮助客户主管节省数小时的规划时间。

Daisy Dool: No new platforms, no steep learning curves, just a smarter. More intentional approach.

Daisy Dool: 没有新平台，没有陡峭的学习曲线，只有一个更聪明、更有目的性的方法。

Daisy Dool: This year, we rolled out a new customer engagement model for our enterprise customer-facing teams, like sales, CS, and PS.

Daisy Dool: 今年，我们为我们的企业客户服务团队，如销售、客户成功（CS）和专业服务（PS）团队，推出了一个新的客户互动模型。

Daisy Dool: The goal was to create greater consistency and alignment in how we support our customers.

Daisy Dool: 目标是在我们支持客户的方式上创造更大的一致性和协调性。

Daisy Dool: Especially in more complex strategic accounts. With that came the need for a more structured and visible way to collaborate across teams. And that's where account planning came in.

Daisy Dool: 特别是在更复杂的战略客户中。随之而来的是对更结构化、更可视化的跨团队协作方式的需求。这就是客户规划的用武之地。

Daisy Dool: As a part of this new model, we introduced account planning as a key motion for context and account plan is a shared document that helps teams rely on customer goals.

Daisy Dool: 作为这个新模型的一部分，我们引入了客户规划作为关键的背景动作，而客户计划是一个共享文档，帮助团队依赖客户目标。

Daisy Dool: 识别风险和障碍，规划关键利益相关者，并记录我们计划如何战略性地与客户互动并发展客户。

Daisy Dool: But very quickly, we realized that creating these account plans, while important, was also really time-consuming. Account executives told us it was taking 3-5 hours, and most of that time was spent summarizing what they already knew, not building strategy.

Daisy Dool: 但很快，我们意识到创建这些客户计划虽然重要，但也非常耗时。客户主管告诉我们这需要3-5个小时，而大部分时间都花在了总结他们已经知道的事情上，而不是制定策略。

Daisy Dool: So we had a critical motion that was meant to support deeper engagement strategy, but it wasn't scaling.

Daisy Dool: 所以我们有一个旨在支持更深层次互动策略的关键举措，但它没有扩展。

Daisy Dool: That was the challenge we needed to solve. We didn't want to throw out the process, we just needed to modernize how we supported it. That's what led us to rethink the workflow using AI.

Daisy Dool: 这就是我们需要解决的挑战。我们不想抛弃这个流程，我们只是需要现代化我们支持它的方式。这就是促使我们使用AI重新思考工作流程的原因。

Daisy Dool: We didn't bring in any new tools, we just leaned into what we already had access to.

Daisy Dool: 我们没有引入任何新工具，我们只是利用了我们已经拥有的资源。

Daisy Dool: For those who may not be familiar, Gong is our conversational intelligence platform. It captures and transcribes customer calls, and then uses AI to surface trends, like what topics are being discussed, how many… how much a customer is speaking, and even indicators of risk or momentum.

Daisy Dool: 对于那些可能不熟悉的人来说，Gong是我们的对话智能平台。它捕捉和转录客户通话，然后使用AI来发现趋势，比如正在讨论什么话题，客户说了多少话，甚至风险或势头的指标。

Daisy Dool: Quip is our collaborative workspace. It's where account executives and other members of customer-facing teams document the account plans. It's live, edible, and in context.

Daisy Dool: Quip是我们的协作工作空间。客户主管和面向客户团队的其他成员在这里记录客户计划。它是实时的、可编辑的，并且与上下文相关。

Daisy Dool: It also integrates directly with Salesforce, so it becomes a part of the workflow, not an extra step.

Daisy Dool: 它还直接与Salesforce集成，因此它成为工作流程的一部分，而不是一个额外的步骤。

Daisy Dool: What we did was introduce a workflow that connects the two.

Daisy Dool: 我们所做的是引入一个连接这两者的工作流程。

Daisy Dool: Gong gives us the insights, and Copilot helps structure those into a draft account plan that's ready for QUIP.

Daisy Dool: 这里的目标不是自动化思考，而是为代表节省总结和格式化的时间，让他们能专注于策略，而且重要的是，每个计划仍然经过人工筛选。

主持人互动：对AI的礼貌

Ketki Yennemadi: Um, so now, it's time for some real talk. While we wait, let's talk about who here says please and thank you to their AI assistants.

Ketki Yennemadi: 那么，现在是时候说点实在的了。在我们等待的时候，我们来谈谈这里有谁会对他们的AI助手说“请”和“谢谢”。

Ketki Yennemadi: How about you, Marina? Do you say please and thank you when you interact with AI?

Ketki Yennemadi: 你呢，Marina？你在与AI互动时会说“请”和“谢谢”吗？

Marina Stojanovic: I do. However, Alexa's the only exception, because she likes to sass me.

Marina Stojanovic: 我会。不过，Alexa是唯一的例外，因为她喜欢对我无礼。

Ketki Yennemadi: Okay.

Ketki Yennemadi: 好的。

Marina Stojanovic: And she doesn't really do what I want her to do, so I don't… I actually argue with her.

Marina Stojanovic: 而且她并不真正做我想让她做的事，所以我不会……我实际上会和她争论。

Marina Stojanovic: Um, but the… if I am typing it into the… into the screen, and it can be traced back to me, I absolutely do, because if they ever become self-aware, I want to be spared. What can I say?

Marina Stojanovic: 但是……如果我把它输入到屏幕上，并且可以追溯到我，我绝对会这么做，因为如果它们有一天变得有自我意识，我希望被幸免。我能说什么呢？

Ketki Yennemadi: Yeah, absolutely, I agree with you. I want to be on their nice list as well.

Ketki Yennemadi: 是的，当然，我同意你的看法。我也想在他们的好人名单上。

Ketki Yennemadi: But here's something I've been reading about. Technically, no, we don't have to be polite to, you know, any AI agent or any AI assistant. Ai doesn't have feelings, no consciousness, or….

Ketki Yennemadi: 但这是我最近读到的一些东西。从技术上讲，不，我们不必对任何AI智能体或AI助手有礼貌。AI没有感情，没有意识，或者……

Ketki Yennemadi: Social expectations. So it doesn't really get offended or even feel appreciated if you keep saying please and thank you.

Ketki Yennemadi: 社会期望。所以如果你一直说“请”和“谢谢”，它并不会真的被冒犯，甚至不会感到被欣赏。

Ketki Yennemadi: However, socially and psychologically, yes, it can be a good idea to be polite to AI, and here's why.

Ketki Yennemadi: 然而，从社会和心理角度来看，是的，对AI有礼貌可能是一个好主意，原因如下。

Ketki Yennemadi: It reinforces empathy, not for AI, but it actually does reinforce empathy and kindness for the person talking to AI.

Ketki Yennemadi: 它增强了同理心，不是对AI，而是实际上增强了与AI交谈的人的同理心和善良。

Ketki Yennemadi: And more importantly, it models good behavior. And, you know, even good language for AI.

Ketki Yennemadi: 更重要的是，它树立了良好的行为榜样。而且，你知道，甚至为AI树立了良好的语言榜样。

Ketki Yennemadi: As AI continues to become more human-like in conversations, polite language might actually help, and it might influence how AI is being trained to respond.

Ketki Yennemadi: 随着AI在对话中变得越来越像人类，礼貌的语言实际上可能会有所帮助，并且可能会影响AI被训练如何回应。

Ketki Yennemadi: So, let's take a look at what our audience thinks. Anything from the audience?

Ketki Yennemadi: 那么，让我们看看我们的观众是怎么想的。观众有什么看法吗？

Marina Stojanovic: A lot of yeses, a lot of yeses. Uh, I heard threatening gives you the best results, but I'm not taking my chance. Good move, Jennifer! I appreciate that.

Marina Stojanovic: 很多“是”，很多“是”。我听说威胁能得到最好的结果，但我不想冒险。干得好，Jennifer！我很欣赏。

Marina Stojanovic: Um, we have Melissa Jackson. I say please before prompt, but I've never said thank you. Uh-oh. It's gonna remember that, Melissa, just wait. Um, if they become self-aware, it's over for Jeff.

Marina Stojanovic: 我们有Melissa Jackson。我在提示前会说“请”，但我从没说过“谢谢”。哦哦。它会记住的，Melissa，等着瞧。如果它们变得有自我意识，Jeff就完蛋了。

Ketki Yennemadi: Very interesting.

Ketki Yennemadi: 非常有趣。

Marina Stojanovic: Sorry, for Jonathan, he read an article that threatening your AI Makes the Prompt Better. My prompts are real good.

Marina Stojanovic: 抱歉，对于Jonathan，他读了一篇文章说威胁你的AI能让提示变得更好。我的提示真的很好。

Ketki Yennemadi: Oh my god. Wow. But here's an interesting angle. I don't know if anyone read about this. There is a cost to being polite to AI. Has anyone read about that article that came out very recently from OpenAI? So, you know, just using phrases like, please, thank you.

Ketki Yennemadi: 天哪。哇。但这里有一个有趣的角度。我不知道有没有人读过这个。对AI有礼貌是有代价的。有人读过OpenAI最近发表的那篇文章吗？所以，你知道，只是使用像“请”、“谢谢”这样的短语。

Ketki Yennemadi: They actually do increase the number of tokens in a prompt, so the number of words increase, therefore it's a very marginal increase. Technically.

Ketki Yennemadi: 它们实际上会增加提示中的令牌（token：AI模型处理文本的基本单位）数量，所以词语数量增加，因此这是一个非常微小的增加。从技术上讲。

Ketki Yennemadi: It's a very small cost, but it does increase the cost.

Ketki Yennemadi: 这是一个非常小的成本，但它确实增加了成本。

Ketki Yennemadi: Um, so there's no official research proving it, but there is some anecdotal data, and I've even heard this in some of the trainings done by Microsoft, that.

Ketki Yennemadi: 所以没有官方研究证明这一点，但有一些轶事数据，我甚至在微软的一些培训中听说过。

Ketki Yennemadi: There is actually, you know, some influence on the model's tone. It doesn't mean if you are nice to the model, it'll give you good responses, otherwise it won't, that's totally not true. However, if you… it tries to mimic your tone. So, if you are more thoughtful, and if you are more polite while asking questions, it might mimic the same tone, and it might lead to better, more thoughtful, or even more nuanced results.

Ketki Yennemadi: 实际上，对模型的语气有一些影响。这并不意味着如果你对模型友好，它就会给你好的回应，否则就不会，那完全不是真的。然而，如果你……它会尝试模仿你的语气。所以，如果你在提问时更周到、更有礼貌，它可能会模仿同样的语气，并可能带来更好、更周到，甚至更细致的结果。

Ketki Yennemadi: So, does anyone here have any experiences with that? Um, while I know politeness doesn't really change the factual accuracy of the data or the results that you get, do you find a subtle change in maybe the tone or the depth of your argument or your engagement with AI? Tell us in the chat.

Ketki Yennemadi: 那么，这里有人有这方面的经验吗？虽然我知道礼貌并不会真正改变数据的真实性或你得到的结果，但你是否发现与AI的互动中，语气或论点深度有细微的变化？在聊天中告诉我们。

Ketki Yennemadi: What do you think? Especially when you're trying to generate something very creative.

Ketki Yennemadi: 你怎么看？特别是当你试图生成一些非常有创意的东西时。

Ketki Yennemadi: 或者当你使用AI，比如写作教练时。写作教练是一个很好的例子，因为它实际上可以创造。

Ketki Yennemadi: Poetry for you, it can create essays for you. So what does that look like? Have you noticed a change?

Ketki Yennemadi: 为你写诗，为你写文章。那是什么样子的？你注意到变化了吗？

Ketki Yennemadi: Tell us in the chat. Let's see what everyone's saying.

Ketki Yennemadi: 在聊天中告诉我们。让我们看看大家都在说什么。

Marina Stojanovic: 做个加拿大人。我喜欢。请继续回应，我们会边走边读。

Ketki Yennemadi: 做个独木舟！我喜欢那个。

Marina Stojanovic: 走错了路，停止生成，对。哦，这就是我要说的。我只想说，是她……是Alexa先开始的，所以，你知道，那不是我的错。她……她就是这样。

Lipsa Mishra: 它也有断言，以确保数据是。

Lipsa Mishra: As it should after the test has run. Um, and then….

Lipsa Mishra: 测试运行后应该的样子。然后……

Lipsa Mishra: And it made some updates. To the trigger handler class.

用例10：Raka Dhar & Julia Groza - AI驱动的元数据生成器

Raka Dhar: So, uh, Julia, if you could start up.

Raka Dhar: 那么，Julia，如果你能开始的话。

Raka Dhar: Hi, everyone! Good afternoon. I am Raka. And along with Julia from engineering, uh, Ben and Tom Zorg, we're excited to walk you through.

Raka Dhar: 大家好！下午好。我是Raka。我和工程部的Julia，以及Ben和Tom Zorg，很高兴能带大家了解。

Raka Dhar: A tool which we have built. And named by ourselves an AI-powered metadata generator.

Raka Dhar: 我们构建的一个工具，我们自己命名为AI驱动的元数据生成器。

Raka Dhar: Now, it sounds scary, but let me simplify it a bit.

Raka Dhar: 现在，这听起来可能有点吓人，但让我稍微简化一下。

Raka Dhar: Metadata is how. Your AI knows it's reading patient records.

Raka Dhar: 元数据是你的AI知道它正在阅读病人记录的方式。

Raka Dhar: And not pizza orders. Think of metadata as the LinkedIn profile for your data, where it's from.

Raka Dhar: 而不是披萨订单。把元数据想象成你数据的LinkedIn个人资料，它来自哪里。

Raka Dhar: What it does, and who to call. Today, we will show you how our tool.

Raka Dhar: 它做什么，以及该联系谁。今天，我们将向你展示我们的工具如何。

Raka Dhar: Automates metadata generation. Helping streamline governance, boost.

Raka Dhar: 自动化元数据生成。帮助简化治理，提升。

Raka Dhar: Transparency, and…. Fast-track our organization's AI readiness.

Raka Dhar: 透明度，并……加速我们组织的AI准备工作。

Raka Dhar: This work right now is in pilot phase for easier understanding, especially for our non-technical audience. We have shared some key terms and definitions in the chat.

Raka Dhar: 这项工作目前处于试点阶段，为了更容易理解，特别是对于我们的非技术观众。我们在聊天中分享了一些关键术语和定义。

Raka Dhar: To follow more comfortably. Now, foiling trusted AI with governed, metadata-rich data.

Raka Dhar: 以便更舒适地跟上。现在，用受治理的、富含元数据的数据来支持可信的AI。

Raka Dhar: Metadata is one of the building blocks. For data governance. In an AI-driven world, your first step is not modeling or building gen AI, it's cleaning up your data closet.

Raka Dhar: 元数据是数据治理的基石之一。在AI驱动的世界里，你的第一步不是建模或构建生成式AI，而是清理你的数据仓库。

Raka Dhar: To build any intelligent. System. Especially….

Raka Dhar: 来构建任何智能系统。特别是……

Raka Dhar: Uh, AI-enabled, responsible application, we need a strong foundation. That starts with data governance.

Raka Dhar: AI赋能的、负责任的应用程序，我们需要一个坚实的基础。这始于数据治理。

Raka Dhar: Ensuring data is secure, well-managed, trustworthy across the organization. You cannot have intelligent, responsible AI without intelligent data.

Raka Dhar: 确保数据在整个组织内是安全的、管理良好的、值得信赖的。没有智能的数据，就不可能有智能的、负责任的AI。

Raka Dhar: Governance is your AI's personal trainer. At the heart of governance is metadata.

Raka Dhar: 治理是你AI的私人教练。治理的核心是元数据。

Raka Dhar: It provides the context, what your data means, where it came from, who owns it, and how it should be used.

Raka Dhar: 它提供了上下文，你的数据意味着什么，它来自哪里，谁拥有它，以及应该如何使用它。

Raka Dhar: To simplify it. Think of metadata as the GPS for your data.

Raka Dhar: 简单来说，把元数据想象成你数据的GPS。

Raka Dhar: Without it, your AI is just driving blind. Is like subtitles for your data.

Raka Dhar: 没有它，你的AI就像在盲目驾驶。它就像你数据的字幕。

Raka Dhar: It helps everyone understand the story, no matter their role. And remember, if AI is the engine.

Raka Dhar: 它帮助每个人理解故事，无论他们的角色是什么。记住，如果AI是引擎。

Raka Dhar: The data governance is the oil. Skip it, and you are heading for a disaster.

Raka Dhar: 数据治理就是机油。跳过它，你就会走向灾难。

Raka Dhar: That's exactly where our tool. Metadata generator comes in, because even the smartest AI cannot go far without a good GPS.

Raka Dhar: 这正是我们的工具——元数据生成器——发挥作用的地方，因为即使是最聪明的AI，没有一个好的GPS也走不远。

Raka Dhar: So far, I have talked about the importance of data governance.

Raka Dhar: 到目前为止，我谈到了数据治理的重要性。

Raka Dhar: And metadata. Now, let's look into this slide. What our tool does.

Raka Dhar: 和元数据。现在，让我们看看这张幻灯片。我们的工具做什么。

Raka Dhar: We have built this using Azure-hosted GPT-4. With enterprise authentication, which makes it flexible enough to work.

Raka Dhar: 我们使用Azure托管的GPT-4构建了这个。通过企业认证，使其足够灵活，可以工作。

Raka Dhar: Not just with SQL-based system. But also with non-SQL data sources. One of the key features of our tool is data lineage.

Raka Dhar: 不仅与基于SQL的系统，也与非SQL数据源。我们工具的一个关键特性是数据血缘（data lineage：追踪数据从源头到最终目的地的整个生命周期）。

Raka Dhar: It shows how data flows, transforms, and connects across systems. Think of it as Google Maps.

Raka Dhar: 它显示了数据如何在系统间流动、转换和连接。把它想象成谷歌地图。

Raka Dhar: For your data pipeline, giving you visibility from source to destination, and every stop in between.

Raka Dhar: 为你的数据管道提供从源头到目的地的可见性，以及中间的每一个站点。

Raka Dhar: Now, let's focus on our features. We have, uh, we use AI.

Raka Dhar: 现在，让我们关注我们的特性。我们有……我们使用AI。

Raka Dhar: To automatically generate plain language descriptions. For tables, views.

Raka Dhar: 自动生成纯语言描述。用于表格、视图。

Raka Dhar: And store procedures. This helps breach the gap between technical metadata.

Raka Dhar: 和存储过程。这有助于弥合技术元数据之间的差距。

Raka Dhar: And business understanding. Second, we have visualized data lineage. So that users can see how data flows transform across system.

Raka Dhar: 和业务理解。其次，我们可视化了数据血缘。这样用户就能看到数据流如何在系统间转换。

Raka Dhar: We added business contacts. Such as suggested data quality improvement.

Raka Dhar: 我们添加了业务联系人。例如建议的数据质量改进。

Raka Dhar: Business term mapping, PHI tagging. To make the metadata actually useful.

Raka Dhar: 业务术语映射，PHI（受保护的健康信息）标记。使元数据真正有用。

Raka Dhar: Finally, we offer export options in both JSON and Markdown. Making it easier to integrate with any tools, documentation, or data catalog.

Raka Dhar: 最后，我们提供JSON和Markdown两种导出选项。使其更容易与任何工具、文档或数据目录集成。

Raka Dhar: And all of these features combined. Create a highly usable, flexible, and intelligent metadata solution.

Raka Dhar: 所有这些特性结合起来，创造了一个高度可用、灵活和智能的元数据解决方案。

Raka Dhar: Ready for AI governance at scale. Now, my colleague, Julia, will walk you through.

Raka Dhar: 为大规模的AI治理做好准备。现在，我的同事Julia将带你了解。

Raka Dhar: How our team previously analyzed metadata. To establish data lineage.

Raka Dhar: 我们的团队以前如何分析元数据来建立数据血缘。

Raka Dhar: Followed by a live demonstration of the tool.

Raka Dhar: 随后是该工具的现场演示。

Julia Groza: Thanks, Raka. So, our team works on a product called Performance Insights.

Julia Groza: 谢谢，Raka。我们的团队正在开发一个名为“性能洞察”的产品。

Julia Groza: Which generates analytics for skilled nursing facilities. Using complex, data-intensive processes.

Julia Groza: 它为专业护理机构生成分析报告，使用复杂、数据密集型的流程。

Julia Groza: Now, developers working on this product often need to understand the precise flow of data.

Julia Groza: 现在，开发这个产品的开发人员经常需要理解精确的数据流。

Julia Groza: By tracing the inputs and outputs for each data table or stored procedure.

Julia Groza: 通过追踪每个数据表或存储过程的输入和输出。

Julia Groza: Now, we have high-level documentation of our data flow process. But before having this tool, it used to be unrealistic to have detailed step-by-step documentation for every single object.

Julia Groza: 现在，我们有我们数据流过程的高层文档。但在拥有这个工具之前，为每一个对象都提供详细的、一步一步的文档是不现实的。

Julia Groza: Mapping this data flow can take a developer up to half a day, costing the company as much as $1,000 each time.

Julia Groza: 映射这个数据流可能需要一个开发人员半天的时间，每次花费公司高达1000美元。

Julia Groza: So this manual process highlights the need for better tools for metadata and data flow analysis.

Julia Groza: 所以这个手动过程凸显了对更好的元数据和数据流分析工具的需求。

Julia Groza: So now we're going to demo our tool and show how we made that process much easier.

Julia Groza: 所以现在我们将演示我们的工具，并展示我们如何让这个过程变得更容易。

Julia Groza: Welcome to the Metadata Generator tool. The first thing that needs to be done when you're working with this tool is you have to be connected to a database. So, I'm connected to one of the databases that we use within our team on Insights.

Julia Groza: 欢迎使用元数据生成器工具。使用这个工具时，首先需要连接到数据库。我已经连接到我们团队在Insights上使用的一个数据库。

Julia Groza: I'm gonna go to the Database Objects tab, and this is where all the action happens. So, I have all of the object types.

Julia Groza: 我要去数据库对象选项卡，这里是所有操作发生的地方。我这里有所有的对象类型。

Julia Groza: That are available in my database. And there's an option to filter by object type.

Julia Groza: 在我的数据库中可用的。还有一个按对象类型筛选的选项。

Julia Groza: And I'm gonna generate metadata and talk about. The descriptions and the data lineage, and how that's being generated within the tool.

Julia Groza: 我将生成元数据并讨论描述和数据血缘，以及它们是如何在工具中生成的。

Julia Groza: So, as that's working, the first thing that's happening is we're getting a plain language description.

Julia Groza: 所以，在它工作的时候，首先发生的是我们得到一个纯语言的描述。

Julia Groza: Of this object, that will give us information on the purpose of the table, business context.

Julia Groza: 关于这个对象，它将为我们提供关于表的用途、业务背景的信息。

Julia Groza: Any relevant tags that could be used later on in machine learning applications.

Julia Groza: 任何相关的标签，这些标签以后可以在机器学习应用中使用。

Julia Groza: And other things. So, the way we're getting this is we're getting all the information about columns, column types.

Julia Groza: 以及其他东西。我们获取这个的方式是，我们获取所有关于列、列类型的信息。

Julia Groza: Primary keys, foreign keys, indexes, and a little bit of sample data from the testing environment.

Julia Groza: 主键、外键、索引，以及来自测试环境的一点样本数据。

Julia Groza: And we're providing that all in a prompt towards the Azure AI service, and we're getting back that metadata description.

Julia Groza: 我们将所有这些信息以提示的形式提供给Azure AI服务，然后我们得到那个元数据描述。

Julia Groza: The second thing that's happening is we're generating a data flow diagram indicating how data is flowing into and out of this object.

Julia Groza: 第二件事是，我们正在生成一个数据流图，指示数据如何流入和流出这个对象。

Julia Groza: You'll see that this information was already generated. But the way this is working in our tool.

Julia Groza: 你会看到这个信息已经生成了。但在我们的工具中，它的工作方式是。

Julia Groza: Is we want to find all of the stored procedures, which are.

Julia Groza: 我们想找到所有的存储过程，它们是。

Julia Groza: Kind of these scripts that modify data within tables. And we want to find all those scripts that change, add, or use information.

Julia Groza: 一种修改表中数据的脚本。我们想找到所有那些改变、添加或使用信息的脚本。

Julia Groza: In this table. These scripts might also get. Data from other tables, so we follow all of those connections step-by-step until we build.

Julia Groza: 在这个表中。这些脚本也可能从其他表中获取数据，所以我们一步一步地跟踪所有这些连接，直到我们构建。

Julia Groza: This network of database objects that you see here. And this is called data lineage.

Julia Groza: 你在这里看到的这个数据库对象网络。这被称为数据血缘。

Julia Groza: And we also look at it the other way around. Not only do we not… not only do we want to know which data flows into the object that we selected, which is this table here.

Julia Groza: 我们也从另一个角度来看待它。我们不仅想知道哪些数据流入我们选择的对象，也就是这个表。

Julia Groza: But we also want to know. How the data from this table is being used in other objects.

Julia Groza: 但我们也想知道这个表中的数据是如何在其他对象中被使用的。

Julia Groza: And the way the tool is doing this is it reads all of the stored procedures, and it finds those source tables and those destination tables and creates those connections.

Julia Groza: 这个工具的做法是，它读取所有的存储过程，找到那些源表和目标表，并创建那些连接。

Julia Groza: So, let's look through the metadata that was generated. We can see that.

Julia Groza: 那么，让我们看看生成的元数据。我们可以看到。

Julia Groza: Here's the plain language description, kind of giving a brief overview.

Julia Groza: 这是纯语言的描述，给出了一个简要的概述。

Julia Groza: Of the table, some business context on why this is important, those relevant tags I was talking about.

Julia Groza: 关于这个表，一些关于它为什么重要的业务背景，以及我之前提到的那些相关标签。

Julia Groza: Some data quality checks, and some insights on the lineage, and some data privacy considerations.

Julia Groza: 一些数据质量检查，一些关于血缘的洞察，以及一些数据隐私考虑。

Julia Groza: In this lineage graph, it's a little bit small right now, but I can go back to….

Julia Groza: 在这个血缘图中，现在有点小，但我可以回到……

Julia Groza: This metadata browser, which shows us. The metadata in a larger.

Julia Groza: 这个元数据浏览器，它向我们展示了更大范围内的元数据。

Julia Groza: Context…. Here we go. So this is the same metadata that we just generated.

Julia Groza: 上下文……好了。所以这和我们刚才生成的元数据是一样的。

Julia Groza: This will just load in a second. So, here we go.

Julia Groza: 这马上就会加载。好了。

Julia Groza: So, our selected object is in purple. And our source tables are in green, and our destination tables are in red.

Julia Groza: 所以，我们选择的对象是紫色的。我们的源表是绿色的，我们的目标表是红色的。

Julia Groza: And our stored procedures. Or those scripts are in orange.

Julia Groza: 我们的存储过程，或者说那些脚本，是橙色的。

Julia Groza: And you can see how data is flowing from this table.

Julia Groza: 你可以看到数据是如何从这个表中流出的。

Julia Groza: Into this table, and how this table is being used in all of these destination tables.

Julia Groza: 进入这个表，以及这个表是如何在所有这些目标表中被使用的。

Julia Groza: And you can start to see how this could take a developer a really long time to do, but is super quick with our tool.

Julia Groza: 你可以开始看到，这可能需要一个开发人员很长时间才能完成，但用我们的工具就超级快。

Julia Groza: Now, you might be thinking, how did the tool do this so quickly? How did it read all these stored procedures and all these database objects and get that information?

Julia Groza: 现在，你可能会想，这个工具怎么能这么快地完成这个？它是如何读取所有这些存储过程和所有这些数据库对象并获取这些信息的？

Julia Groza: So when I first started this application and ran it, there was a background process that was occurring that was reading.

Julia Groza: 所以当我第一次启动并运行这个应用程序时，有一个后台进程正在发生，它正在读取。

Julia Groza: All of these stored procedure objects. And extracting the source and destination tables using AI.

Julia Groza: 所有这些存储过程对象。并使用AI提取源表和目标表。

Julia Groza: And we store all of that information. In our database. So something really important about this tool is that everything that's AI-generated.

Julia Groza: 我们存储所有这些信息。在我们的数据库中。所以关于这个工具，非常重要的一点是，所有AI生成的东西。

Julia Groza: Is then saved in our database. We do this because excessive calls to the AI service can become time-consuming and costly. So.

Julia Groza: 然后被保存在我们的数据库中。我们这样做是因为对AI服务的过多调用可能会变得耗时且昂贵。所以。

Julia Groza: An AI response is only generated once per object, and then it's reused every time thereafter, because we can have many people.

Julia Groza: 每个对象只生成一次AI响应，之后每次都会重复使用，因为我们可以有很多人。

Julia Groza: Generating metadata descriptions for the same objects, and we don't want to make repeated calls.

Julia Groza: 为相同的对象生成元数据描述，我们不想进行重复调用。

Julia Groza: So you can see that that's indicated by this flag here, that this metadata is up-to-date.

Julia Groza: 所以你可以看到，这里的这个标志表明，这个元数据是最新的。

Julia Groza: No regeneration needed. If the database object was updated, this would be.

Julia Groza: 无需重新生成。如果数据库对象被更新，这将是。

Julia Groza: Warning you that you should probably regenerate the metadata. Another thing that I want to share is….

Julia Groza: 警告你可能应该重新生成元数据。另一件我想分享的是……

Julia Groza: Our…. Ai model specifically looks at column names to see.

Julia Groza: 我们的……AI模型专门查看列名来判断。

Julia Groza: If any… there's any PHI, potentially, in these tables. So, you can see that.

Julia Groza: 这些表中是否可能包含任何PHI（受保护的健康信息）。所以，你可以看到。

Julia Groza: I selected another table. Um, the metadata description immediately came up, because this is also saved in the database. We don't need to generate it again.

Julia Groza: 我选择了另一个表。元数据描述立即出现了，因为这也保存在数据库中。我们不需要再次生成它。

Julia Groza: And you can see that we might have potential PHI in the physician first name, middle name, etc.

Julia Groza: 你可以看到，我们可能在医生的名字、中间名等方面有潜在的PHI。

Julia Groza: And the user should be aware of this. The second thing I want to show you with this tool is our schema comparison feature.

Julia Groza: 用户应该意识到这一点。我想向你展示的这个工具的第二个功能是我们的模式比较功能。

Julia Groza: Now, the purpose of this feature is. If you're working with multiple database objects, and you want to understand the difference between them, whether it be structure-wise or business context-wise.

Julia Groza: 现在，这个功能的目的是。如果你正在处理多个数据库对象，并且你想了解它们之间的差异，无论是结构上还是业务背景上。

Julia Groza: It's helpful to be able to compare them. So, I'm gonna pick two schemas, and when I'm picking two schemas.

Julia Groza: 能够比较它们是很有帮助的。所以，我准备选择两个模式，当我选择两个模式时。

Julia Groza: The tool is finding all of the common objects between them that can be compared.

Julia Groza: 该工具正在查找它们之间所有可以比较的共同对象。

Julia Groza: And it's doing this based on naming conventions. So, as you can see here.

Julia Groza: 它是基于命名约定来做的。所以，正如你在这里看到的。

Julia Groza: Um, these two object names…. Are similar to each other, except for that schema.

Julia Groza: 这两个对象名……彼此相似，除了那个模式。

Julia Groza: Name difference. So when I go ahead and compare schemas…. This is already saved to the database as well, like I mentioned, we save all the responses in the database.

Julia Groza: 名称差异。所以当我继续比较模式时……这也已经保存到数据库中了，正如我提到的，我们把所有的响应都保存在数据库中。

Julia Groza: We get a summary of differences on the parameters, the objects used within this.

Julia Groza: 我们得到了关于参数、其中使用的对象的差异摘要。

Julia Groza: Particular object, any differences in logic. I'll put columns, as well as some risks and recommendations for working with these.

Julia Groza: 特定对象，任何逻辑上的差异。我会列出列，以及一些使用这些对象的风险和建议。

Julia Groza: Two objects. So, overall, this tool is very helpful for developers to get better business context on database objects.

Julia Groza: 两个对象。所以，总的来说，这个工具对开发人员更好地了解数据库对象的业务背景非常有帮助。

Julia Groza: It's preparing the data, giving it relevant tags that could be used later on in those machine learning applications.

Julia Groza: 它正在准备数据，给它相关的标签，这些标签以后可以在那些机器学习应用中使用。

Julia Groza: And the most important thing is it's developing that data lineage and showing that data flow.

Julia Groza: 最重要的是，它正在开发数据血缘并展示数据流。

Julia Groza: Which is imperative when you're building on top of or modifying your data flow transformation.

Julia Groza: 当你在构建或修改你的数据流转换时，这是至关重要的。

Julia Groza: Welcome to….

Julia Groza: 欢迎来到……

Julia Groza: Okay. Uh, so…. Based on the database that was demoed in that video, which is specific to.

Julia Groza: 好的。所以……基于那个视频中演示的数据库，它是特定于。

Julia Groza: Our product, Performance Insights. Um, that database has roughly 1,000 database objects.

Julia Groza: 我们的产品，性能洞察。那个数据库大约有1000个数据库对象。

Julia Groza: So, this tool has the potential to save. 250 to 4,000 hours in developer time.

Julia Groza: 所以，这个工具有潜力节省250到4000小时的开发人员时间。

Julia Groza: And $60,000 to a million dollars in cost savings. And again, this is just for one database for insights alone.

Julia Groza: 并节省6万到100万美元的成本。再次强调，这仅仅是针对一个洞察数据库。

Julia Groza: So, our goal with this tool is to make this tool available to all engineering teams.

Julia Groza: 所以，我们这个工具的目标是让所有工程团队都能使用这个工具。

Julia Groza: For their respective databases. So everyone can benefit from the same time and cost savings.

Julia Groza: 为他们各自的数据库。这样每个人都能从同样的时间和成本节省中受益。

Julia Groza: Uh, and for our non-engineering teams, we hope we provided another example that you can take away from this symposium.

Julia Groza: 对于我们的非工程团队，我们希望我们提供了另一个例子，你们可以从这次研讨会中带走。

Julia Groza: On how to break down complex, repetitive workflows. And use AI for well-defined steps along the way.

Julia Groza: 关于如何分解复杂、重复的工作流程，并在过程中使用AI来完成定义明确的步骤。

Julia Groza: Now, we have several planned enhancements to make this tool even more valuable.

Julia Groza: 现在，我们有几个计划中的增强功能，以使这个工具更有价值。

Julia Groza: The first one is that we want to increase the granularity of that data lineage graph.

Julia Groza: 第一个是，我们想增加那个数据血缘图的粒度。

Julia Groza: So right now, it's tracking the data flow across tables. But we want to make it track the data flow across columns. So this is going to give developers better visibility into how changes to individual columns.

Julia Groza: 所以现在，它正在跟踪跨表的数据流。但我们想让它跟踪跨列的数据流。这将让开发人员更好地了解单个列的更改如何。

Julia Groza: Can impact the entire system. Next, we want to improve our metadata itself.

Julia Groza: 影响整个系统。接下来，我们想改进我们的元数据本身。

Julia Groza: And divide it into business, technical, and operational metadata. So it's more actionable for different types of users.

Julia Groza: 并将其分为业务、技术和运营元数据。这样对不同类型的用户来说更具可操作性。

Julia Groza: And finally, we want to expand even the reach of this tool beyond databases.

Julia Groza: 最后，我们甚至想将这个工具的范围扩展到数据库之外。

Julia Groza: We'd love for this tool to be able to document the data flow for any kind of repository that has some kind of data flow, which is a lot of repositories.

Julia Groza: 我们希望这个工具能够为任何有数据流的知识库记录数据流，而这样的知识库有很多。

Julia Groza: When it comes to responsible AI. The most important part of our project is that we're saving every AI-generated result.

Julia Groza: 当谈到负责任的AI时。我们项目最重要的部分是，我们保存每一个AI生成的结果。

Julia Groza: With timestamps, enabling full review and auditability. And when we do prompt the Azure AI service, we're creating highly specific, context-rich prompts.

Julia Groza: 带有时间戳，实现全面的审查和可审计性。当我们提示Azure AI服务时，我们正在创建高度具体、上下文丰富的提示。

Julia Groza: With standardized inputs and standardized outputs, allowing us to control the generated response as much as we can.

Julia Groza: 通过标准化的输入和标准化的输出，让我们能尽可能地控制生成的响应。

Julia Groza: But most of the logic in this tool is handled by deterministic code that us as developers can review.

Julia Groza: 但这个工具中的大部分逻辑是由我们作为开发人员可以审查的确定性代码处理的。

Julia Groza: So, after completing this project, we have two key takeaways. One is that AI is most effective when you have a strong understanding of what it's generating.

Julia Groza: 所以，在完成这个项目后，我们有两个关键的收获。一个是，当你对AI生成的内容有深刻的理解时，AI是最有效的。

Julia Groza: It's easy to rely on AI suggestions without grasping the underlying libraries in your code, for example.

Julia Groza: 很容易依赖AI的建议，而没有掌握你代码中底层的库，例如。

Julia Groza: But we found that reviewing documentation and then guiding the AI ultimately saved us more time than prompting it without sufficient context.

Julia Groza: 但我们发现，审查文档然后指导AI，最终比在没有足够上下文的情况下提示它节省了我们更多的时间。

Julia Groza: And lastly, I keep talking about this point, but we found that AI works best for small, well-defined tasks, because it allows us to maintain control.

Julia Groza: 最后，我一直在谈论这一点，但我们发现AI最适合处理小的、定义明确的任务，因为它让我们能保持控制。

Julia Groza: And validate results as we go. So, thank you so much for attending this demo, and thank you to the AI Symposium team for giving us the opportunity to share this with all of you.

Julia Groza: 并在过程中验证结果。所以，非常感谢你们参加这次演示，也感谢AI研讨会团队给我们机会与大家分享这个。

Julia Groza: 我们可以回答你们提出的任何其他问题。谢谢。

Kate Kaplya: Okay, wonderful. So, good afternoon, everyone. My name is Kay Calia, and I'm an implementation consultant.

Kate Kaplya: 显示4周的数据。关于这个仪表盘，需要注意的一点是，它包含宏元素，Copilot无法分析，所以在运行分析之前必须将其转换为常规的Excel工作簿。

Kate Kaplya: So why is this use case important? Um, in terms of impact, we're looking at increased consultant efficiency when preparing post-goal life recommendations.

Kate Kaplya: 那么为什么这个用例很重要呢？在影响方面，我们看到在准备实施后建议时，顾问的效率提高了。

Kate Kaplya: Consultants can reclaim time, saving up to 20% of an 8-hour workday when preparing metrics for four facilities daily.

Kate Kaplya: 顾问们可以节省时间，每天为四个设施准备指标时，可以节省高达8小时工作日的20%。

Kate Kaplya: We also have standardized improvement planning across facilities, allowing for continuous workflow optimization.

Kate Kaplya: 我们还在所有设施中标准化了改进规划，从而实现了持续的工作流程优化。

Kate Kaplya: And last but not least, this empowers implementation team with actionable insights and direct access to support materials.

Kate Kaplya: 最后但同样重要的是，这为实施团队提供了可操作的洞察和直接访问支持材料的途径。

Kate Kaplya: Leading to increased productivity and capacity to process three times more facilities in the same amount of time.

Kate Kaplya: 从而提高了生产力，并能在相同时间内处理三倍多的设施。

Kate Kaplya: Um, in terms of lessons learned, uh, you do want to make sure to use very specific and detailed prompts outlining what information to analyze.

Kate Kaplya: 在经验教训方面，你确实要确保使用非常具体和详细的提示，概述要分析什么信息。

Kate Kaplya: Including, but not limited to, facility and workflow needs names or specific metrics.

Kate Kaplya: 包括但不限于设施和工作流程的名称或特定指标。

Kate Kaplya: And, um, linking metrics to resources was also identified as an area of improvement, um, as Copilot was unable to extract resources directly stored within the customer support portal. For example, it is possible to pull in smart zone eCourses, however, that information was only pulled from the documents that were found in Shared Workspaces.

Kate Kaplya: 而且，将指标与资源链接也被确定为一个改进领域，因为Copilot无法直接从客户支持门户中提取资源。例如，可以提取智能区域的电子课程，但这些信息只从共享工作区中找到的文档中提取。

Kate Kaplya: It also may pull personal cloud files and email attachments from my experience.

Kate Kaplya: 根据我的经验，它也可能提取个人云文件和邮件附件。

Kate Kaplya: Um, resources and recommendations need detailed review to confirm that they apply to the facility-specific workflows. For example, you want to take into account differences between the skilled nursing facility versus an assisted living facility.

Kate Kaplya: 资源和建议需要详细审查，以确认它们适用于特定设施的工作流程。例如，你需要考虑到专业护理机构和辅助生活机构之间的差异。

Kate Kaplya: Um, how it kind of help others. Uh, point-click here, so by linking metrics to specific how-to guides and resources, AI acts as a dynamic navigator, bridging data and resources.

Kate Kaplya: 它如何能帮助他人。在这里，通过将指标与特定的操作指南和资源链接起来，AI扮演了一个动态导航员的角色，连接了数据和资源。

Kate Kaplya: Which in turn reduces training gaps and improves adoption. Different prompts can be utilized to access training resources and recommendations for learning and development in customer support teams.

Kate Kaplya: 这反过来又减少了培训差距并提高了采用率。可以利用不同的提示来访问培训资源和客户支持团队学习与发展的建议。

Kate Kaplya: And it also accelerates post-school life monitoring, so co-pilots can automate that first layer of post-go-life review.

Kate Kaplya: 它还加速了实施后的监控，所以Copilot可以自动化实施后审查的第一层。

Kate Kaplya: Flagging trends and surfacing support materials. And this model can be replicated across other workflows, such as billing for implementation, customer success, and account management teams.

Kate Kaplya: 标记趋势并提供支持材料。这个模型可以复制到其他工作流程中，比如实施、客户成功和客户管理团队的计费。

Kate Kaplya: Uh, for responsible use of AI, you do want to make sure to validate the recommendations against facility-specific nuances.

Kate Kaplya: 为了负责任地使用AI，你确实要确保根据特定设施的细微差别来验证建议。

Kate Kaplya: So you want to approve, edit, or annotate the plan before actually sharing it with the facility.

Kate Kaplya: 所以在实际与设施分享之前，你想要批准、编辑或注释这个计划。

Kate Kaplya: And you also want to review the reference sources to check for PHI or project data, specifically focusing on items that are used by Copilot to generate recommendations and supporting materials.

Kate Kaplya: 你还想审查参考来源，以检查是否存在PHI（受保护的健康信息）或项目数据，特别关注Copilot用于生成建议和支持材料的项目。

Kate Kaplya: And finally, you want to refine your AI prompts or adjust your metric thresholds based on the generate responses.

Kate Kaplya: 最后，你想要根据生成的响应来优化你的AI提示或调整你的指标阈值。

Kate Kaplya: As risk thresholds may vary from project to project. Um, in conclusion, this use case allows to reduce the amount of time spent on analyzing metrics to prepare for monitoring sessions.

Kate Kaplya: 因为风险阈值可能因项目而异。总而言之，这个用例可以减少分析指标以准备监控会议所花费的时间。

Kate Kaplya: Freeing up time for strategic outreach. It also shows how AI can transform raw post-implementation data into actionable insights.

Kate Kaplya: 从而腾出时间进行战略性外展。它还展示了AI如何能将原始的实施后数据转化为可操作的洞察。

Kate Kaplya: Um, enabling teams to make faster evidence-based decisions without the manual analysis.

Kate Kaplya: 使团队能够在没有手动分析的情况下，更快地做出基于证据的决策。

Kate Kaplya: Which ensures more efficient reviews, improved care outcomes, and a future-ready approach to continuous improvement.

Kate Kaplya: 这确保了更高效的审查、改善的护理成果，以及一个面向未来的持续改进方法。

Kate Kaplya: And I will now open the floor for any questions.

Kate Kaplya: 我现在开放提问环节。

主持人互动：AI解释政策

Auroosa Kazmi-Ishaq: 好的，完美。我把这个放进去。好的，那么，在我们等待下一位演讲者准备的时候。

Since it's trained on all of the feature sets and functionality of Pharmacy Connect, you can just ask it to describe that to you.

用例13：Jennifer Magana, Maja Madirazza, Krisika Suthan & Charley Yang - Figma与Copilot在UX设计中的应用

Jennifer Magana - Product: Yeah, thanks everyone. Hi, uh, Charlie, Maya, Krisika, and I from User Research and Design are excited to share.

Jennifer Magana - 产品部: 是的，谢谢大家。嗨，我是用户研究与设计部的Charlie、Maya、Krisika和我，我们很高兴能分享。

Jennifer Magana - Product: How we're partnering with AI to help us move faster, spot insights sooner, and make our work more inclusive.

Jennifer Magana - 产品部: 我们如何与AI合作，以帮助我们更快地行动，更早地发现洞察，并使我们的工作更具包容性。

Jennifer Magana - Product: So let's get started. Um, today we're focusing on that early phase of product development.

Jennifer Magana - 产品部: 那么让我们开始吧。今天我们关注的是产品开发的早期阶段。

Jennifer Magana - Product: When we're still figuring out what to build, it's what we call product discovery.

Jennifer Magana - 产品部: 当我们还在弄清楚要构建什么时，我们称之为产品发现。

Jennifer Magana - Product: This phase is often overwhelming. Ideas are slow to form. Research findings are shared too late, and collaboration happens, but in silos.

Jennifer Magana - 产品部: 这个阶段通常是压倒性的。想法形成缓慢。研究发现分享得太晚，协作虽然发生，但却是孤立的。

Jennifer Magana - Product: That's why we're rethinking how we explore and align. We're learning how to partner with our AI tools we call Design Pals.

Jennifer Magana - 产品部: 这就是为什么我们正在重新思考我们如何探索和协调。我们正在学习如何与我们称之为“设计伙伴”的AI工具合作。

Jennifer Magana - Product: To change how we collaborate and build with more confidence. We each give it a role to play.

Jennifer Magana - 产品部: 来改变我们的协作方式，并更有信心地进行构建。我们每个人都给它分配一个角色。

Jennifer Magana - Product: Maya will showcase her ideation coach.

Jennifer Magana - 产品部: Maya将展示她的构思教练。

Maja Madirazza: Sigma Make is our new AI-powered ideation coach. It helps us remix ideas quickly and explore multiple design directions to solve user problems.

Maja Madirazza: Figma Make是我们新的AI驱动的构思教练。它帮助我们快速重组想法，并探索多种设计方向来解决用户问题。

Maja Madirazza: I recently used it to explore how users could indicate the location of documentation within an assessment.

Maja Madirazza: 我最近用它来探索用户如何在评估中指示文档的位置。

Maja Madirazza: Instead of sketching, I use prompts to generate a design that closely matched what I had in mind.

Maja Madirazza: 我没有画草图，而是使用提示来生成一个与我心中所想非常匹配的设计。

Maja Madirazza: Being the design helped me uncover a new challenge. How might we help users not just select a progress note, but select the right one?

Maja Madirazza: 这个设计帮助我发现了一个新挑战。我们如何能帮助用户不仅是选择一个进度笔记，而是选择正确的那个？

Maja Madirazza: So for the next round, I adjusted the prompt to include more context, like, who wrote the note.

Maja Madirazza: 所以在下一轮，我调整了提示，加入了更多的上下文，比如，谁写的笔记。

Maja Madirazza: Their role, and the date. Then I realized, wouldn't it be better if users could actually preview the entire node before selecting it?

Maja Madirazza: 他们的角色和日期。然后我意识到，如果用户在选择之前能实际预览整个笔记，会不会更好？

Maja Madirazza: I then added a preview feature. Now, when users click preview, the note expands, allowing.

Maja Madirazza: 然后我添加了一个预览功能。现在，当用户点击预览时，笔记会展开，允许。

Maja Madirazza: Allowing them to read it fully before linking it. As you can see, Figma Make helped me ideate quickly, think visually, and iterate on the fly.

Maja Madirazza: 让他们在链接之前完整地阅读它。正如你所看到的，Figma Make帮助我快速构思，进行视觉化思考，并即时迭代。

Maja Madirazza: Turning one idea into three different variations, I could share with the product team.

Maja Madirazza: 将一个想法变成三个不同的变体，我可以与产品团队分享。

Maja Madirazza: With that, I'll pass it over to Christika.

Maja Madirazza: 就此，我把话筒交给Christika。

Krisika Suthan: Okay, so now I'll talk about our next design pal, AI as an interaction slash prototyping partner. Here is a mock-up. It's helpful for aligning with product, engineers, and even users, but one screen doesn't show the full experience. It's hard to grasp functionality and flow from a static image. Normally, this is where we designers prototype, but often we don't always have the time.

Krisika Suthan: 好的，现在我来谈谈我们的下一个设计伙伴，AI作为交互/原型设计伙伴。这是一个模型。它有助于与产品、工程师甚至用户对齐，但一个屏幕无法展示完整的体验。从静态图像中很难把握功能和流程。通常，这是我们设计师制作原型的地方，但我们往往没有时间。

Krisika Suthan: Or clinical context to build something that is realistic. Here is where we use Figma Make.

Krisika Suthan: 或者没有临床背景来构建一些现实的东西。这就是我们使用Figma Make的地方。

Krisika Suthan: So using Figma Make, I turned this mock-up into a working prototype in just over a half hour. It does not match our evergreen design system or core, and that is okay.

Krisika Suthan: 所以使用Figma Make，我在半个多小时内就把这个模型变成了一个可工作的原型。它与我们的常青设计系统或核心不匹配，但这没关系。

Krisika Suthan: What it does do is bring the mock-up to life, helping us visualize interaction, workflow, and realistic content scenarios.

Krisika Suthan: 它所做的是让模型活起来，帮助我们可视化交互、工作流程和现实的内容场景。

Krisika Suthan: In our recent exploration, we used this to quickly align with product managers on key ideas. But looking ahead, there is potential to use these prototypes for user testing and end-to-end.

Krisika Suthan: 在我们最近的探索中，我们用它来快速与产品经理就关键想法达成一致。但展望未来，这些原型有潜力用于用户测试和端到端的。

Krisika Suthan: Evaluation of feasibility. Passing it down to Jennifer.

Krisika Suthan: 可行性评估。现在交给Jennifer。

Jennifer Magana - Product: Thanks, Krisika. Discoverly is an insight translator. It's an AI agent I've customized in Copilot to help me share research findings in real time. I'll show you how it works.

Jennifer Magana - 产品部: 谢谢，Krisika。Discoverly是一个洞察翻译器。这是我在Copilot中定制的一个AI智能体，用来帮助我实时分享研究发现。我来展示一下它是如何工作的。

Jennifer Magana - Product: Um, before Discoverly, we talked to customers, highlighted transcripts, summarized key points, created themes and insights, and then presented the findings.

Jennifer Magana - 产品部: 在Discoverly之前，我们与客户交谈，高亮转录稿，总结要点，创建主题和洞察，然后展示发现。

Jennifer Magana - Product: Now, we're still talking to customers and highlighting transcripts, that part's not going to change.

Jennifer Magana - 产品部: 现在，我们仍然在与客户交谈并高亮转录稿，那部分不会改变。

Jennifer Magana - Product: Um, think of it like data labeling. Basically, it's helping the AI interpret that data accurately.

Jennifer Magana - 产品部: 把它想象成数据标注。基本上，它是在帮助AI准确地解释那些数据。

Pawandeep Kaur: In March 2023, PointClicker acquired the patient pattern as a strategic investment to advance value-based care and better.

Pawandeep Kaur: 2023年3月，PointClicker收购了Patient Pattern，作为一项战略投资，以推进基于价值的护理并更好地。

Pawandeep Kaur: Drive better patient outcomes. Following the early exists launch in April 2024, stewardship of the product transitioned to our engineering team.

Pawandeep Kaur: 推动更好的患者结果。在2024年4月早期版本发布后，产品的管理权移交给了我们的工程团队。

Pawandeep Kaur: Who brought strong expertise in Java and related technologies. It became clear that while the product offered substantial potential, it also presented several unforeseen challenges that require careful attention moving forward.

Pawandeep Kaur: 他们在Java和相关技术方面拥有强大的专业知识。很明显，虽然该产品提供了巨大的潜力，但它也带来了一些意想不到的挑战，需要我们在前进中仔细关注。

Pawandeep Kaur: From the outset, we recognized there were significant challenges hidden beneath the surface.

Pawandeep Kaur: 从一开始，我们就认识到表面之下隐藏着重大的挑战。

Pawandeep Kaur: The system had become complex over time. With quick fixes, workarounds, and evolution from PCC standards, making improvements slow and unpredictable.

Pawandeep Kaur: 随着时间的推移，系统变得复杂。由于快速修复、变通方案以及与PCC标准的演变，使得改进变得缓慢且不可预测。

Pawandeep Kaur: The front end, inspired by patient pattern theme, lacked PCC co-design styles.

Pawandeep Kaur: 前端，受Patient Pattern主题启发，缺乏PCC的协同设计风格。

Pawandeep Kaur: Resulting in an inconsistent user experience. While learning a new language like Python and Django wasn't a challenge, adapting to the way frameworks were implemented created any extra hurdles for us.

Pawandeep Kaur: 导致用户体验不一致。虽然学习像Python和Django这样的新语言不是挑战，但适应框架的实现方式给我们带来了额外的障碍。

Pawandeep Kaur: Routine changes started to require significant efforts, and often impacted our performance, reliability, and scalability.

Pawandeep Kaur: 常规的变更开始需要巨大的努力，并经常影响我们的性能、可靠性和可扩展性。

Pawandeep Kaur: Making it clear that we needed a more scalable, unified foundation to deliver improvements faster and more confidently.

Pawandeep Kaur: 这清楚地表明，我们需要一个更具可扩展性、更统一的基础，以便更快、更自信地交付改进。

Pawandeep Kaur: That's when we decided to try something different, and bring AI into our transformation journey.

Pawandeep Kaur: 那时我们决定尝试一些不同的东西，并将AI引入我们的转型之旅。

Pawandeep Kaur: We just two engineers, we rebuilt the platform in three focus phases, all powered by AI.

Pawandeep Kaur: 我们只有两名工程师，我们在三个重点阶段重建了平台，全部由AI驱动。

Pawandeep Kaur: First, we used GitHub Copilot and CloudSonnen to untangle the maze.

Pawandeep Kaur: 首先，我们使用GitHub Copilot和CloudSonnen来解开这个迷宫。

Pawandeep Kaur: Mapping workflows, doing class-by-class comparisons, and building testament blueprints. This let everyone, engineers and business folks, get streamlined.

Pawandeep Kaur: 映射工作流程，进行逐类比较，并构建测试蓝图。这让每个人，无论是工程师还是业务人员，都能简化流程。

Pawandeep Kaur: Next, put up those blueprints and put AI to work. Migrating key modules.

Pawandeep Kaur: 接下来，拿出那些蓝图，让AI开始工作。迁移关键模块。

Pawandeep Kaur: From Python to Java, modernizing the front end with React, and connecting it all with mermaid diagrams, so we could catch issues early.

Pawandeep Kaur: 从Python到Java，用React现代化前端，并用Mermaid图（一种用于生成图表和流程图的标记语言）将所有东西连接起来，这样我们就能及早发现问题。

Pawandeep Kaur: In just one week, we had a working prototype. Finally, we polish the product.

Pawandeep Kaur: 仅仅一周，我们就有了可工作的原型。最后，我们打磨产品。

Pawandeep Kaur: Iterating plot, performance gains, and catching security vulnerabilities. Beyond the speed, what stood out most was the clarity and assurance AI brought to our design.

Pawandeep Kaur: 迭代情节、性能提升和捕捉安全漏洞。除了速度，最突出的是AI为我们的设计带来的清晰度和保证。

Pawandeep Kaur: And making decisions. And how it was making our decisions.

Pawandeep Kaur: 并做出决定。以及它如何做出我们的决定。

Pawandeep Kaur: Very impactful. So what's… what did this transformation mean for our team and our users?

Pawandeep Kaur: 非常有影响力。那么……这次转型对我们的团队和用户意味着什么？

Pawandeep Kaur: First, this transformation could reduce development effort from one's estimated at 400 engineering hours.

Pawandeep Kaur: 首先，这次转型可以将开发工作量从估计的400个工程小时减少。

Pawandeep Kaur: To just 20, allowing us to deliver value to customers weeks sooner.

Pawandeep Kaur: 到仅仅20小时，让我们能提前数周向客户交付价值。

Pawandeep Kaur: With improvement testing and streamlined workflows, we can lower support. Needs and could strengthen user trust.

Pawandeep Kaur: 通过改进测试和简化的工作流程，我们可以降低支持需求，并能增强用户信任。

Pawandeep Kaur: Our system could handle twice the workload on the same hardware without degrading the expected latency.

Pawandeep Kaur: 我们的系统可以在相同的硬件上处理两倍的工作负载，而不会降低预期的延迟。

Pawandeep Kaur: We were able to automate 30% of repetitive tasks, which was one of our greatest wins.

Pawandeep Kaur: 我们能够自动化30%的重复性任务，这是我们最大的胜利之一。

Pawandeep Kaur: These benefits are based on measurable gains we saw in our pilot version, demonstrating what's possible as we scale these improvements.

Pawandeep Kaur: 这些好处是基于我们在试点版本中看到的可衡量收益，展示了当我们扩展这些改进时可能实现的目标。

Pawandeep Kaur: 回顾过去……有几个教训非常突出。

Pawandeep Kaur: 首先，规划我们的工作流程带来了巨大的变化。它将不确定性变成了清晰。

Pawandeep Kaur: Second, AI is a powerful tool. For speed and scale, but it's the expertise of our people that ensures quality.

Pawandeep Kaur: 其次，AI是一个强大的工具。在速度和规模方面，但确保质量的是我们员工的专业知识。

Pawandeep Kaur: 最后，快速的胜利很重要。每一个小成功都会建立势头，并帮助团队保持参与。

Pawandeep Kaur: 这种方法并非我们旅程独有。任何PCC团队都可以采取这些步骤，让工作可见，将AI与人类判断相结合。

Erik Stabile: 我们与Rafat Rajudin部分合作，使用Copilot Studios来解决我们在推出新的安全增强功能时面临的一个挑战。

Erik Stabile: Uh, for point-click care customers.

Erik Stabile: 为PointClickCare的客户。

Erik Stabile: Uh, when we launched our latest round of security enhancements, we were flooded with questions from internal support teams.

Erik Stabile: 当我们推出最新一轮的安全增强功能时，我们收到了来自内部支持团队的大量问题。

Erik Stabile: Customer success managers and customers. But the answers…. Were often complex and specific. They were scattered across multiple resources, making it difficult for teams to find consistent, timely information, slowing down response times and increasing support overhead.

Erik Stabile: 客户成功经理和客户。但答案……通常复杂且具体。它们分散在多个资源中，使得团队难以找到一致、及时的信息，从而减慢了响应时间并增加了支持开销。

Erik Stabile: To solve this problem, we introduced an AI-powered agent embedded directly in Microsoft Teams and trained on all of our relevant customer-facing content.

Erik Stabile: 为了解决这个问题，我们引入了一个直接嵌入到Microsoft Teams中的AI驱动的智能体，并用我们所有相关的面向客户的内容对其进行了训练。

Erik Stabile: Now, instead of digging through lengthy FAQs, guides, and slide decks, team members could simply ask the AI.

Erik Stabile: 现在，团队成员不必再翻阅冗长的常见问题解答、指南和幻灯片，他们可以直接问AI。

Erik Stabile: And receive context-aware responses. This reduced response times, improving consistency, and freeing staff to focus on higher-value work.

Erik Stabile: 并收到具有上下文感知的回应。这减少了响应时间，提高了信息的一致性，并让员工能专注于更高价值的工作。

Erik Stabile: Um, since launch, the agent has powered 150-plus sessions with a 75% engagement rate.

Erik Stabile: 自推出以来，该智能体已支持超过150次会话，参与率达到75%。

Erik Stabile: 在内部用户中获得了5分制中的4分满意度。

Erik Stabile: 在现场办公时间，我们每周都会举办办公时间，回答客户关于MFA（多因素认证）的问题。

Erik Stabile: 在Copilot Studio中，知识源与生成式答案协同工作。当你添加一个知识源时，你的智能体可以利用企业数据，无论它来自内部系统。

Lisa Jarrett: 所以当我们推进我们产品的AI部分时。

Lisa Jarrett: Um, it's… they're looking to us. To do the testing and do the work, and make it transparent, and make it understandable, and do the risk management that's associated with it.

Lisa Jarrett: 他们指望我们。去做测试，去做工作，让它透明，让它易于理解，并做与之相关的风险管理。

Lisa Jarrett: 对正在使用的数据源保持透明。所以有很多不同的维度。

Lisa Jarrett: 你不是一次性做完RAI（负责任的AI）。你在整个生命周期中都要做，并且要持续做。
